Representatives Returning to Shanghai after Petitioning on the Reform of Customs Administration Issues 119

▲ Luo Qinghua Makes a Statement

More than ten representatives, including Lu Wenshao, Luo Qinghua, Tu Kaizheng, Zheng Chengqing, and Xie Zhongle, who were sent by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and various industry associations to petition in Beijing on customs administration issues, returned to Shanghai last night after being delayed until last night. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency specially inquired about the process and received a detailed reply from Mr. Luo Qinghua, a representative of the petitioning delegation, who expressed his views on the case. The details are recorded below:

▲ Petition Process: The representatives arrived in Beijing on the morning of the 27th and went to the Central Party Headquarters, where they were received by Committee member Ye Chucang. Mr. Ye deeply regretted that the lack of appropriate laws and regulations in customs administration had led to the current disputes. He believed that the points requested by the Shanghai merchants were essential and agreed to submit them to the Central Political Committee for discussion. He also said that Shanghai's industry and commerce were extremely depressed after the One-Two-Eight Incident, and the central government was deeply concerned. It was planning how to maintain the status quo and could not bear to see further destruction. Therefore, although the Central Party Headquarters is not a direct administrative organ, it would base its decisions on the principle of full sympathy and send a letter to the National Government, ordering the competent authorities to investigate and correct the situation. The representatives were satisfied. They then went to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, where they were received by Director Zhang Yichou of the Commercial Department because Minister Chen had gone to Ma'anshan to survey mines. They were received by Director Peng Xuepei of the General Affairs Department at the Executive Yuan. All of the points in the petition were fully accepted. Director Peng also said that the customs would absolutely apply the Administrative Procedure Law. If merchants suffered losses due to excessive fines or illegal searches, they could file complaints with the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance to recover the losses. Yesterday, they went to the Ministry of Finance, where they were jointly received by Vice Minister Li Tiaosheng and Section Chief Wu of the Customs Administration. After the representatives stated their petition, Vice Minister Li said that the Ministry of Finance had not heard of the recent actions taken by the customs in Shanghai. Section Chief Wu explained that the scope of the customs' authority to search merchants' goods was limited to the customs location and the customs offices that had been registered with the customs. As for breaking into stores to search, the Customs Administration was also surprised to hear about it. He asked the representatives to tell the affected merchants to report the facts truthfully, and the Ministry of Finance would definitely investigate the matter impartially. The people's absolute right to apply the Administrative Procedure Law to customs is unquestionable and the tariff law is also being drafted, but it is a major matter and cannot be completed overnight. At the Legislative Yuan, they were received by Secretary-General Zhang Weihan. Mr. Zhang believed that the establishment of a tariff law would not only provide merchants with laws to follow and be protected, but also reduce malpractices and supplement national revenue. He agreed to submit it to the meeting for discussion and to engage in drafting it. The representatives then went to the Nanjing Chamber of Commerce to inform them of the process and then went to Zhenjiang in the afternoon. The Jiangsu-Shanghai People's Food Conference was held in Zhenjiang, and representatives from various chambers of commerce in Jiangsu Province attended the meeting. They were informed of the recent actions taken by the Shanghai Customs and the petition process, and they all expressed their deep sympathy and agreed to advocate for a unified position. The representatives completed their missions and returned to Shanghai this afternoon.

▲ Representatives' Statement: Luo Qinghua, Executive Committee member and Director of the Commercial Department of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, was one of the representatives of the Chamber of Commerce who went to Beijing this time. When asked about his views on the case by the reporter, Luo replied that customs duties are a legitimate national revenue and the duty that the people should bear. Tax evasion directly damages the national treasury, and indirectly allows unscrupulous people to take advantage of loopholes, causing the market to lose its balance, which is particularly harmful. As for how tax evasion occurs, the causes are far-reaching and the situation is complex, which cannot be explained in a few words. The significance of our petition this time is to establish a tax law and fundamentally eliminate the malpractices of tax evasion. Customs officials are paid by the state and should fulfill their responsibilities. If a large amount of smuggling occurs, the customs officials should at least feel guilty. However, the customs should exercise its authority within the limits of its name, that is, within the customs. Even if we take a step back, it can only investigate the importer with the responsibility of paying taxes and obtain proof of taxpayer qualification, but it cannot conduct searches in Chinese stores that sell retail. According to the words of Section Chief Wu of the Customs Administration, it can be seen that searching stores is indeed unfounded. Article 10 of the Provisional Constitution states that "The people's residences shall not be entered, searched, or sealed without legal basis." When the customs searched the Shichangtai Watch Company on August 31, it is said that they did not show a search warrant at that time. It was not until September 2 that the Customs Commissioner sent a letter to the First Special District Court through the Customs Superintendent. The customs is a national tax collection agency, and customs officials are government employees. Our country is a country ruled by law. If customs officials are outside the law, how can merchants and the people have nowhere to turn? The main cause of this phenomenon is the lack of specific laws and regulations for customs duties. For example, there is a Consolidated Tax Law for the consolidated tax, a Business Tax Law for the business tax, and a Salt Tax Law for the salt tax. However, the customs duty, which is the largest source of national revenue, lacks legal regulations, which is a pity. Fortunately, the Yuan and ministries have expressed their intention to start drafting laws, and the Administrative Procedure Law has also been applied to customs. Therefore, merchants and the people will have protection and remedies in the future. Merchants and the people in Shanghai have always taken it upon themselves to be patriotic and law-abiding, and they should encourage each other to avoid being used as a pretext.

Shen Shuyu Came to Shanghai Yesterday 120

▲ To Discuss Measures to Prevent Tax Evasion

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has recently stated that there are no specific laws and regulations for customs administration. Customs officials, restricted by procedures such as consular visas for foreign merchants, do not fully exercise their authority when goods are imported, nor do they investigate foreign firms that directly order goods. Instead, they conduct searches on Chinese merchants who have transferred goods repeatedly, and even lead a large number of armed detectives to guard stores and detain merchants' goods, causing great pain to merchants and the people throughout the city. The representatives of the chamber of commerce and various industries, including Lu Wenshao, Zheng Chengqing, Jin Runxiang, and Luo Qinghua, went to Beijing on the evening of the 26th to petition the central government, requesting that customs officials be prevented from searching stores and that illegal penalties by customs be promulgated. After receiving the presentation, the Ministry of Finance specially sent Shen Shuyu, Director of the Customs Administration, to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday. It is said that Mr. Shen is scheduled to meet with representatives of various industries in the city within a few days to discuss proper measures to prevent tax evasion and investigate the situation of forced searches by customs officials in order to stop them.

Zhu Tingqi Came to Hubei to Inspect Salt Affairs 121

▲ Significant Progress Has Been Made

Mr. Zhu Tingqi, Director-General of the Salt Affairs Audit Office, along with Chief Inspector Zeng Yangfeng, passed through the Pinghan Railway and arrived in Hubei from Henan. In recent days, he has personally visited the Hubei Coast Audit Office, the Hubei Coast Transport Bureau, the Hankou Weighing and Releasing Office, the Tax Police Bureau, the Hanyang Salt Warehouse, and the wheel transport wharf for on-the-spot inspections, and has given additional encouragement to the employees of various institutions. It is reported that the salt affairs on the Hubei coast have made significant progress since the merger of administrative agencies. The annual expenses have been reduced by nearly 300,000 yuan, and the tax revenue for the first nine months of this year has increased compared to the same period last year. The various bad practices of salt merchants and Huai salt merchants have been completely eliminated, and the prices of both refined salt and Huai salt have been reduced as a result. The procedures for transporting salt have been simplified, the efficiency of public affairs has been greatly improved, and merchants and the people have felt more convenient. It is also reported that as a result of the inspection by Mr. Zhu and others, there are concrete plans to prohibit private smuggling and promote legitimate salt sales, which will be implemented soon. It is also reported that Mr. Zhu and others will go to Changsha to inspect within a few days.

Establishment of the National Joint Conference of All Circles for National Salvation 122

▲Opening Ceremony Held Yesterday

With the Japanese army invading our Eastern Provinces, national sentiment has been boiling. The National Joint Conference of All Circles for National Salvation, initiated by national salvation organizations from various provinces, held its inaugural meeting yesterday at 9:00 AM at the Zhou Family Garden on Jing'an Temple Road. A total of 102 representatives from various provinces and cities, including Long Xiangsan, Zhang Zhiyuan, Zhang Jie, Shen Zurong, Feng Guo, Xie Naishi, Zhang Junguang, Zuo Hua, and Chen Zhenquan, attended. The details of the meeting are as follows:

▲Meeting Proceedings (1) Music played to commence the meeting; (2) All stood at attention; (3) The Party Song was sung; (4) The most respectful salute was paid to the national flag of the Party and the portrait of the late Premier; (5) The Chairman respectfully read the late Premier's will; (6) A moment of silence was observed to mourn the compatriots in the Northeast who had suffered hardship; (7) The presidium was elected. In addition to Zhang Junguang, Zuo Hua, and Chen Zhenquan, as decided by the preparatory committee, with Tu Liang as the Secretary-General of the conference, the other four members were elected by the conference: Zhang Zhihuan, Shen Zurong, Feng Dong, and Zhang Jie; (8) The Chairman of the presidium delivered an opening address; (9) A report on the preparatory process was presented; (10) Proposals were discussed. Eleven people were elected by the conference to form a proposal review committee to first organize and review the proposals before submitting them to the conference for discussion. The afternoon was devoted to the proposal review committee.

▲Chairman's Speech Zhang Junguang, the Chairman of the presidium, delivered the opening address, saying: "Fellow representatives, under the invasion and oppression of Japanese imperialism, resisting Japan and saving the nation is the duty of our people. The reason for the establishment of this conference, and the only task after its establishment, is to earnestly save the nation and resist Japan. However, the mission of this conference is currently not limited to the single aspect of resisting Japan and saving the nation. There are still many important responsibilities for national salvation that we must address in conjunction. Therefore, the task of this conference is even heavier, and the members of this conference should also make redoubled efforts to shoulder this heavier task. In these days of deepening national crisis, when the nation is on the verge of collapse, and the aggression of Japanese imperialism in the three northeastern provinces is becoming more blatant and aggressive, our government still does not know to rise up and resist. The volunteer army is fighting bloody battles in the bitter cold outside the Great Wall, but there is no substantial assistance from within the Great Wall. The warlords of Sichuan and Shandong only know to engage in internal strife and infighting, and political factions are fighting and undermining each other all day long, while the national morale is declining and the organization is disintegrating. Under such a terrible situation, even the desire to resist Japan and save the nation is impossible. Based on this understanding and need, the members of this conference, in order to save the national crisis, will make every effort to promote this great union of national salvation organizations from all circles across the country. On the one hand, we will consolidate the strength of the people to serve as a backing for the government, and on the other hand, we will prepare to fight against Japanese imperialism with real strength. On the other hand, we will oppose the evil forces that harm the nation and promote domestic unity and peace. Only in this way can we save the overturning of the collapsing situation, relieve the people from their suffering, and secure the country on a solid foundation. This is the only proposition of this conference, and it is also the main reason for convening this national representative conference today. I hope that the representatives present will use our spirit and enthusiasm to work hard to save the nation. This is not only the good fortune of this conference, but also the good fortune of the Republic of China."

▲Report on the Preparatory Process Chen Zhenquan, recommended by the preparatory committee, reported on the preparatory process, saying: "Fellow representatives, the purpose and task of this conference have just been explained in detail by Mr. Zhang Junguang, so I don't need to repeat them. Now, I will simply report to you the process of the preparation of this conference. The task of this conference is to focus on practical resistance to Japan and national salvation, and to unite the people of the whole country. Therefore, during the preparatory period, this conference has been working hard on the organization and union of various places throughout the country. During the three-month preparatory period, representatives were sent to various places to solicit comrades. For more distant places, such as Yunnan, Guizhou, Sichuan, Gansu, and the Northeast provinces, we contacted them by post and telegraph, and asked them to immediately send representatives to reside in Shanghai so that we could meet face to face and work together. The national salvation organizations and patriotic people in various places, upon seeing the propositions of this conference, were of course very enthusiastic to participate. Therefore, in just over a month and a half, the first step of our membership solicitation procedure has been completed. The representatives who went to various places have returned to Shanghai one after another, and groups from distant provinces have also sent representatives to Shanghai. In total, in the past three months, more than 50 organizations and more than 100 people have come to participate in the organization. The foundation of the organization of this conference has been consolidated. This is the first stage of the preparation of this conference. After the organization of this conference had a foundation, we began the second stage of work. The work of this period was not completed until now, which is the organization, arrangement, and planning of various organizations, the drafting and discussion of the program and constitution, and finally the preparation for this conference. Although the work during this time was very trivial, it was also very important. It was only in a very short period of less than a month that we completed the task of preparing for the present, and the undertaking is now concluded. However, all the important tasks of this conference still require all members to work together to complete."

▲Proposal Review At 2:00 PM, the proposal review committee was convened. The attendees were Zhang Guangjun, Zuo Hua, Chen Zhenquan, Zhang Zhiyuan, Shen Zurong, Feng Guo, Zhang Jie, Huang Nanxi, Xie Naishi, Long Xiangsan, Dong Mosheng, Tan Jingyu, and Tu Liang, totaling 13 people. Zhang Junguang, Long Xiangsan, and Xie Naishi were elected as the military proposal review group. Chen Zhenquan, Tan Jingpin, Tu Liang Zuo, and Hua were elected as the political proposal review group. Zhang Zhiyuan, Zhang Jie, and Shen Zuru were elected as the diplomatic proposal review group. Huang Nanxi, Feng Guo, and Dong Mosheng were elected as the economic proposal review group. Each group reviewed the proposals, totaling 25 items. By 5:00 PM, all the items that had not been completely reviewed would be discussed tomorrow morning.

Monument Installation Ceremony for the Martyred Colleagues of the Two Railways 124

▲Scheduled to be Held on November 3rd

During the January 28th Anti-Japanese War, the Songhu Railway and the eastern section of the Jinghu Railway were strategically important. When the soldiers of the 19th Route Army bravely fought against the enemy, the employees of the two railways were dedicated to their duties in transporting and supplying military food, often disregarding the dangers in the midst of gunfire and continuing their work as usual. As a result, 14 people were martyred. Their loyalty, bravery, and sincerity are comparable to those of the fallen soldiers. After the war subsided, the employees of the two railways donated funds to create a bronze monument to the martyred employees, which was decided to be placed at various stations to commemorate them and to alert the people of the country. It has been decided that the monument installation ceremony will be held simultaneously at various stations at 10:00 AM on the morning of the third day of next month.

▲Monuments Placed at Various Stations A total of two large and six small monuments will be erected. One large monument will be erected opposite the station inspection office at the Shanghai North Station and one at the Nanjing Station. The six small monuments will be erected at the stations where the martyrs died. The director of the bureau, Director Chen, the chief of the Transportation Department, Zheng Zizhao, and the chiefs of the various sections will preside over the monument installation ceremonies at the various stations. The names, locations, and dates of the martyrdom of the martyred employees are as follows, according to an investigation by a reporter from the Huadong News Agency: Station Master Ji Youqing, colleagues Ye Keqing and Zhang Jinyin, martyred on February 7 at the Yuncaobang Station on the Songhu Railway; Trackman Zhang Wenkui, martyred on February 8 at the Zhanghuabang Station on the Songhu Railway; Trackman Gao Shaoquan, Station Clerk Zhang Rongsheng, and Gatekeeper Fan Hongsheng, martyred on January 29 at the Tiantong'an Station on the Songhu Railway; Gatekeeper Tian Rongfu, Zhang Hua, martyred on January 29 at the Baoshan Road Station on the Songhu Railway; Station Master Xu Bin on February 21, Flagman Xue Sanlang on February 11, and Clerk Wang Jingxian on February 24, successively martyred at the Nanxiang Station on the Jinghu Railway; Station Clerk Xuan Quandan, martyred on February 25 at the Zhenru Station on the Jinghu Railway; Trackman Zhu Yonglin, martyred on February 29 at the Xinlonghua Station on the Huhang Railway.

The Japanese Xinzeng Store Was Bombed Twice Yesterday 127

▲Hand Grenade Hit the Door Panel

▲Smoke Filled the Air and Passersby Fled

The Japanese Xinzeng Foreign Goods Store at 114-116 Fa Da Ma Road was bombed once on September 19 this year. No one was injured, only a few floorboards and glass were damaged. Unexpectedly, less than two months later, it was bombed for the second time yesterday. On the 27th of this month, the store received a warning letter. At about 6:15 PM yesterday, just as the store door was being closed, an uninvited guest kept knocking on the door. For the sake of prudence, the shop assistants did not answer. The person then left. About a quarter of an hour later, the sound of knocking on the door was heard again. The shop assistants peered out through the crack and saw that it was a familiar customer. They opened the door to let him in. Unexpectedly, just as the customer stepped into the doorway, a hand grenade came from across the road and hit the fifth and sixth door panels in the center. With a loud bang, the surrounding area shook. A corner of the door panel was destroyed, and smoke filled the air. Passersby fled, and the order was disrupted. The Dada Mingzhong Police Station was nearby and immediately sent detectives to investigate. They collected the damaged grenade shell and took it to the police station for investigation.

Butcher Gangs Stage Bloody Feud

▲ Jiangbei Gang Members Assault People from Beiping

The Shandong Gang and the Jiangbei Gang, both groups of butchers, have harbored deep-seated grudges due to disputes over the purchase of pigs. Recently, conflicts between members of the two gangs have frequently occurred, resulting in mutual killings. Yesterday morning around 11:00 AM, two butchers from Beiping, Chen Cuiqing and Hua Zhenhai, who worked at a butchery located at No. 12 Tianhou Lane, Yuezhou Road, in the Public Concession, took a tram from the northern part of the city to the south. They got off at the Oil Depot Wharf, intending to go to a pig market there to select pigs. Unexpectedly, just as they got off the tram and had taken only a few steps, more than 30 members of the Jiangbei Gang, led by Wang Guirong, swarmed up and indiscriminately attacked the two men with axes and iron rulers. In an instant, both men were covered in wounds and bleeding profusely, collapsing into a pool of blood in extreme pain. Chao Yueshun and others from the 18th patrol post in the area heard of the incident and rushed to the scene. By then, the Jiangbei Gang members had scattered and fled, with only Wang Guirong being apprehended. Wang was taken to the first precinct's first station for interrogation, while the two injured men were taken to the hospital for treatment. It is said that the injuries of both men are severe, and their lives may be in danger.

Anhui associations in Shanghai have scheduled a meeting to discuss all matters related to opposing the rice license fee. The notice issued by the associations is as follows: "Regarding the Anhui Provincial Government's continued imposition of the rice license fee, which is seen as a continuation of Chen Tiaoyuan's disastrous administration that harms the people, our associations believe it is illegal and detrimental to the people. We have separately telegraphed the State Council and relevant ministries, urging them to order its abolition, and have also telegraphed chambers of commerce in Wuhu, Bengbu, and other cities in the province to unite and oppose it. It is now scheduled for November 1st (Tuesday) at 2:00 PM, at the Atlantic Restaurant on the Fourth Road, with refreshments prepared, to hold a general meeting of Anhui natives in Shanghai to discuss detailed measures to address this issue. Representatives will be elected on the spot to petition in both Beijing and Wuhan. This matter concerns the vital interests of the Anhui people, and we hope you will attend on time."

Banditry in Tangwan Township

Several bandits descended upon Zhoujiazhai in the Erqu area of Tangwan Township in the western suburbs the other night. When they were robbing the homes of villagers in Gaojiali, Lin Bin, the deputy head of the township's defense corps, and Yang Hui, an officer from the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau, were leading the corps and police on patrol. They heard the commotion in the village and rushed to the scene. The bandits had already plundered the wealth of Zhou Ahai, Wang Xingen, and others, and were escaping with their loot, traveling along the Pu River by boat. The corps and police were unable to pursue them due to a lack of boats. They then searched for the remaining bandits in the surrounding villages. They arrived at Peicai Township at dawn. According to villagers such as Zhang Guisheng, a suspicious boat was docked at the Daliu Port. The corps and police investigated and found a boat, but no one was on board. It was abandoned by the Roman bandit gang. After searching the boat, they found the boat's registration papers and other items. The boat was impounded and guarded, and the authorities began investigating the whereabouts of the bandits to apprehend and punish them.

Ding Weiyue Jailed for Illegal Possession

▲ Sentenced to Six Years in Prison

Xu Yongyuan, a Chinese detective at the Huishan Police Station, previously discovered that Ding Weiyue, a constable residing at No. 1926 Dongyouheng Road, was illegally possessing prohibited items at his home. Xu and a Western detective secretly went to Ding's residence and arrested him, finding four bullets and sixty yuan in counterfeit banknotes from a certain bank. The number of days he was detained before the final judgment was determined to be credited at a rate of two days of detention for one day of imprisonment. The bullets and counterfeit banknotes were confiscated.

Water Damage to Water Chestnut Boat After Striking Stone Bridge

Water chestnuts from the Xinshi area of Huzhou, Zhejiang Province, have long enjoyed a strong reputation. Every early winter, merchants would send their employees with funds to purchase water chestnuts from the locals and load them onto boats, which would then be towed by small steamers to Shanghai for sale. This practice has become commonplace. The other day, a small steamer (i.e., a gasoline boat) was towing two boats loaded with water chestnuts from Xinshi to Shanghai when it sped up to try to get to Shanghai first and cash in on the market. However, as it sped near the Shaxi Long Bridge, about five li from Xinshi, the second boat struck the bridge stones due to excessive power. The bow of the boat was smashed, and water immediately flooded in, causing it to sink. The sailors on board fell into the river. Fortunately, the water chestnut boats were mostly without cargo holds, and the sailors were good swimmers. The steamer stopped and rescued the sailors, preventing any fatalities. However, the water chestnuts on board, worth more than 300 yuan, were all dumped into the river. Yesterday, the steamer arrived in Shanghai and reported the incident to the cargo owners for handling.

Chen Zixiang Dies by Suicide

Chen Zixiang, a 30-year-old native of Zhejiang, had been staying in Room 27 of the Dahua Hotel at No. 85 Xixinqiao Street in the French Concession for 45 days. Recently, he introduced a fellow villager to work as a waiter at the Nanjing Hotel. The prospective waiter had entrusted Chen with 450 yuan to pass on, but Chen secretly used the money himself. Now, the prospective waiter had come to Shanghai to inquire whether the job had been secured, which caused Chen to feel ashamed and desperate, leading him to take his own life by poisoning himself at the hotel the other night. It was not until 1:00 PM yesterday that the waiter noticed Chen was in critical condition. He was immediately taken to Renji Hospital, but due to the severity of the poisoning, treatment was ineffective, and he died at 3:30 PM. The hospital reported the incident to the police station, who sent detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall mortuary for an autopsy. As there were no relatives of the deceased, the police will report the case to the court for inspection.

Robbery Case Verdict

Sun Jinman, a 20-year-old Jiangbei native, residing at No. 404 Pingmin Public Housing, Xietu Road, in the Chinese Concession, was found on the morning of the 14th of this month carrying two six-inch Browning pistols and sixteen bullets, intending to deliver them to his accomplices Li Xiaosizi and Shen Xiaosizi in Hongkou for a robbery. While passing the intersection of Weierjia Road and Ailaige Road in the French Concession, he was discovered and apprehended by Chinese and Western detectives from the special agency of the French Police Station. The pistols and bullets were confiscated. It was found that Sun's gang had robbed the Xieshunchang Tobacco and Paper Shop at No. 51 Xujiahui Road, as well as the Mahongji Cleaning Bureau and the Xietai Coal Shop at No. 754 Malang Road, all in the French Concession. After being transferred to the Second Special Court, Wang Gangxu, the presiding judge of the criminal court, opened the trial and declared the debate closed. The previous morning, Judge Wang presided over the First Criminal Court and sentenced Sun Jinman to eight years of imprisonment for each of the three counts of armed robbery with three or more accomplices, and three years of imprisonment for the crime of possessing military pistols and bullets with the intent to commit a crime. The sentences are to be served concurrently for a total of twelve years. The number of days he was detained before the final judgment was determined to be credited at a rate of two days of detention for one day of imprisonment. The two pistols, sixteen bullets, and two shell casings were confiscated. The defendant was transferred to the detention center.

▲ Chen Youcai Kidnaps Wang Zhaodi

▲ Soldiers Liu Kun and Others Follow

Wang Zhaodi, a 14-year-old native of Changzhou and sister of Wang Genda, who resides at No. 151 Guangzhao Road, Zhabei, works in a silk factory. Special Article Judge Tang's Research Report on the Situation of the Shanghai Public Concession Volume 4 (8)

Deliberation on Governance and Reporting

What needs to be directly understood is that the organization of a city must be regarded as a whole organic entity, and all distinctions between them are only superficial. This kind of organic entity has several molecules, but each of these molecules is actually a part of a whole entity. Every action related to governance contains two elements, namely, will, or original power, and the method of execution or implementation. In theory, the determination of action is different from the execution of action, but in practice, from the establishment of a resolution to the implementation of the resolution, it is a whole action. Looking at the nature of the British municipal organization, it can be seen that the origin of the resolution lies in the citizen representatives of the city council or committee. The real basis and element of the city government is the original power of the representative body, rather than the purely mechanical work of executing the will of the representative body. The will belongs to the city council that has been entrusted with power, and the will owned by the agent of the city council is only secondary. The actual governance work is usually determined by the resolution of the committee, which is undoubtedly true, but the city council can still freely intervene at any time and refuse to approve it, thus invalidating the resolution of the secondary group and replacing the wrongly expressed will of its lower-level agent with its own higher will."

The Relationship Between the City Council and the Committee

"One level that must always be remembered is that each committee is a molecule of an entity, a hand and foot of the city council, not a separate agency, but a member of a larger agency. Not only is the committee a limb of the city council, but also according to the municipal government organization law, each member of the committee is also a part of the city council. Not only is the committee a smaller-scale city council with its own special functions, but the city council still retains its full original power after the committee is established. Suppose this kind of power is more rarely exercised in the city council, it is because of the recognition that the committee and its staff have a special opportunity to constitute a proper decision in its administrative part in charge. In general, the city council can always expand and contract the scope of authority of the committee at will, and can control the operation of the committee with ordinary rules and special resolutions.

At the same time, the various committees and their staff are by no means merely the instruments of the city council. The decision of the city council is the final ruling, but it is wrong to regard the city council as a worker, and its various committees or its staff as the instruments used by the worker to work. Except for the questions of policy organization that need to be decided, the committee can proceed according to its own design and is rarely interfered by the superior agency. This is probably true, and it is probably true for the committees in large cities. In theory, it would be easy for a councilor to make difficulties for the committee and disrupt its plans when the city council meets every month, but in practice, the difficulties in theory have not occurred, because every city councilor is a committee member and knows that he should trust other committees other than his own, and must trust them. A sense of responsibility arises from trust, and trust and responsibility are the six key points for appropriate measures.

The Relationship Between the Committee and the Staff

The relationship between the committee and its staff reflects the relationship between the city council and the committee. The people of the mainland often have the concept of regarding officials as high-ranking figures, but the British do not have this tendency or need. Except in the courts, Congress, and in etiquette and social aspects for the British King, the British have not seen a high position in their minds. Those who are appointed and paid by the representatives of cities or rural areas to implement and execute the law have no high status. On the other hand, the officials of the city government, although their position cannot make their treatment particularly different from what their fellow citizens enjoy, but if they can engage in work that is beneficial to the people anywhere in the UK, they can obtain a full sense of appreciation. Those with expert knowledge and skills can also get the respect they deserve. The respect received by the senior officials of the city government, as well as the trust of the committee, the city council, and even the general public in the various officials, is purely due to their character, ability, and the importance of their work, not due to the official position held by the various officials. It is rare for officials to be the subject of mutual attacks between political factions. Although there is a relationship between political skills and the appointment of officials, or a relationship with resignation, although the latter is very rare, the motives for such appointments and removals are not announced. The characteristic of the British civil service system is unwavering loyalty to the frequently transferred political officers. The merits of the facilities of various parts of the government are attributed to the political officers of the reading parts, and if there is a mistake, it is also the responsibility of the officer in charge. If his subordinates are attacked, the political officer in charge will come forward to defend them. The power exercised by the permanent staff over their administrative officers is often very great. This administrative officer, in terms of the city government,

Administrative Yuan Orders Jiangsu Provincial Government to Investigate and Abolish Pig Tax 134

The pork traders of various counties in Jiangsu Province, in opposition to the establishment of checkpoints by the Jiangbei Jingrutai and other county business tax bureaus to collect pig taxes, organized a temporary representative joint association. They sent representatives Qi Wenyao and others to the capital and province to petition and requested the Shanghai Municipal Council to prepare a memorial to be personally delivered by the representatives. This was previously reported. Now, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has forwarded Directive No. 226 from the Executive Yuan, stating that the Jiangsu Provincial Government has been instructed to investigate and abolish the tax. This is for your information. After receiving the directive, the joint association has already informed the pork merchants in Jiangbei.

Zhabei Defense Corps Prepares for Winter Defense 135

The Third Defense Post of the First Team of the Shanghai North District Security Corps, due to its remote location, convened a corps affairs meeting at 2 PM on October 30th to prepare for winter defense in advance. More than thirty people attended, chaired by Da Jianhong. After performing the ceremonial rites, it was resolved to submit a report for supplementary military supplies in advance, awaiting orders to be deployed for defense. Several important cases were also discussed. Zhang Jingxian, the person in charge of the post, recognizing the importance of winter defense, specially obtained approval from the corps headquarters to recruit ten volunteer corps members from today to fill vacancies and solidify strength. Any individual aged between eighteen and thirty with a decent occupation and no vices, willing to serve the local area, is welcome to join. The post's address is No. 1, Wu Lu Li, Taiyang Temple Road, Gonghe Xin Road.

Sakonji Holds Farewell Banquet for Japanese Residents Yesterday 136

According to the Far East News Agency, Sakonji, the commander of the Japanese Third Fleet, held a grand farewell party yesterday at 11 AM on the flagship "Izumo" as he is about to return to his country. A total of more than forty Japanese officials and residents attended. During the banquet, Sakonji expressed his gratitude for the support of the Japanese residents and stated that after returning home, he would earnestly contribute to the party authorities' policy of protecting Japanese residents. The representative of the Japanese Residents' Association stood up to thank him. The gathering ended joyfully at 3 PM. It is said that Sakonji's departure is scheduled to occur after the arrival of Vice Admiral Takahashi, the incoming commander of the Third Fleet.

▲ Fourth time held

The Shanghai County Farmers' Education Center held a cattle plowing competition for the purpose of improving the health of cattle, increasing work efficiency, and ensuring the safety of farmers' lives. The competition has been held three times before. The following is a summary of the meeting:

Yun Huifang's Appeal Case Scheduled for Trial 140

▲ Letter of appeal has been submitted to the court.

▲ Trial set for December 21st

Yun Huifang, a member of the "Blood Soul Eliminate Traitors" group, angered by traitorous merchants privately selling Japanese goods and undermining the boycott movement, sent letters and bombs to the Cotton Cloth Association and the Yongchang Coal Store and Maochang Foreign Goods Store on Xin Zha Road, warning them. She was arrested by Chinese police officers in the Chinese concession and taken to the French Concession Police Department, who handed her over to the Second Special District Local Court. The court sentenced her to one month in prison but, considering that she was under sixteen years old, granted probation. Subsequently, the Public Concession Police Department transferred her to the First Special District Local Court, which sentenced her to one year in prison and allowed her to be released on bail. All of this has been previously reported. Yun, at the time of the sentencing, stated that she did not accept the verdict. Soon after, her representative lawyer filed an appeal. The First Special Court submitted the case file to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court for handling. It is recently learned that Yun's lawyer has submitted the letter of appeal to the Second Branch of the Higher Court. Yu Hua, the presiding judge of the criminal division of the court, considering the importance of the case and the need to expedite its handling, has scheduled a special trial for 1 PM on December 21st in the first courtroom. Subpoenas for the witnesses to appear in court have also been issued and ordered to be delivered by the police.

Fire Indemnity Association in Disaster Area Urges Prompt Adoption of Public Bond Measures 141

The Shanghai Fire Insurance Indemnity Promotion Association for the disaster area, after the Chinese insurance companies approved the public bond measures, convened a full executive committee meeting at the Ningbo General Chamber of Commerce on Edward Road at 1 PM yesterday. More than twenty people attended, including Fang Jiaobo, Wang Xianhua, Chen Songyuan, Tang Youwei, Gu Zhuxuan, Mo Meiqing, and Ye Xiaoshan. Fang Jiaobo chaired the meeting, and the meeting was conducted according to procedures. First, Tang Youwei reported on the recent developments in the association's affairs and the proposed implementation plans. Then, various cases were discussed. (1) A letter was sent to the Chinese managers of the foreign insurance companies, requesting them to explain the advantages and disadvantages to the foreign directors in detail. (2) It was decided that committee members Tang Youwei and Mo Meiqing would attend the meetings of the Claims Settlement Committee as non-voting members. (3) A document was submitted to the Social Bureau urging the prompt adoption of a public bond scheme. The document stated, "Submitting this document for requesting matters, we have respectfully received your bureau's instruction No. 4963. Upon reading it, we found that only the Chinese companies have approved the issuance of public bonds to resolve the fire insurance indemnity in the disaster area, while the foreign companies have not yet expressed their opinions, which is regrettable. We urge your bureau to take strict measures to negotiate so that the Chinese and foreign companies can reach a consensus. Otherwise, the tens of thousands of victims in the affected area will pledge to provide backing and continue the struggle. We await further instructions on how to proceed. As for the details of the public bond scheme, such as the method and regulations, we respectfully request your bureau to promptly formulate a detailed plan (or instruct the representatives of the accounting firm who originally proposed the scheme to draft it) and announce it so that the outside world can understand it and facilitate smooth progress. We also request that the insurance companies be thoroughly reorganized and that regulations and restrictions be implemented as soon as possible so that they can complement the public bond scheme and benefit all. This document is respectfully submitted by Yu Qiaqing, Fang Shubo, Chen Songyuan, Wang Xianhua, Mo Meiqing, Tang Youwei, Wang Binyan, and others to Wu, the Director of the Shanghai Social Bureau."

Wang Xunfu Involved in Kidnapping Case with Widow 143

▲ Defendant allegedly negotiated ransom and inquired about the situation.

▲ Shot in the waist while escaping, then captured.

Wang Xunfu, a native of Yangzhou residing in a bungalow on Yucai Road in the Chinese concession, is implicated in a case involving a group of armed individuals who kidnapped Wang Yu, a widow from Shaoxing, from her residence at No. 71, Tai'an Lane, Beishan West Road, around 11 PM on January 10th of this year. They also robbed her of valuables worth $270. He was detained by Detective Shen Chongli of the Hongkou Police Department and brought before the First Special District Court for questioning and detention. Judge Shen Bingrong of the Third Criminal Court conducted an inquiry the other day. Attorney Zhang Tianyin of the Police Department stated that during the reinvestigation, it was discovered that prior to the incident, Jiang Dinghui, who has already been arrested and executed, invited him to the Qixin Inn on Fuzhou Road to conspire with Xiao Wang, Li Xiuyu (who has already died), and others to rob Wang Yu's property. After kidnapping her, they hid her in a house at No. 560, Dixiwei Road, and sent letters to her relatives demanding a ransom of $100,000. Around 10 PM on the 19th of the month, he and Jiang Dinghui, Wang Xianqiao, and others went to the vicinity of the intersection of Edward Road and Jiangxi North Road to negotiate the ransom with the widow's representatives. They resisted the police officers with gunfire. Xiao Wang and Li Xiuyu were killed on the spot. The defendant was shot in the waist and escaped, but was finally captured on the 26th at the Xieqiao Hospital in the French Concession after being treated by Dr. Guo Renji. The medical expenses totaled $38.50. He left the hospital on February 12th. The police previously found a gray robe with bullet holes at his home, which the defendant was wearing when he was negotiating on Edward Road, as well as evidence of the group's resistance to arrest at the time. Zhang Yunsheng, a Chinese detective from No. 320, Dixiwei Road Police Department, Shang Wu, a Chinese detective from the Huishi Police Department, and the victim, Wang Yu, were all summoned to court for questioning. The gray silk robe was presented for examination, and the bullet holes were clearly visible. According to Wang Yu's statement, prior to the incident, on January 1st, a woman claiming to be surnamed Lin and Li Xiuyu (who has already died) came to rent a room behind the living room. After a few days, Xiao Wang also came. On the evening in question, she, along with her relative Wang Jiliang and a woman surnamed Luo who lived with her, were playing mahjong upstairs when Lin and Li Xiuyu came upstairs under the pretext of borrowing a pen. They immediately produced guns and threatened them. Lin dragged her downstairs and pushed her into her bedroom, where she was monitored by the defendant and another unknown person armed with guns. After a while, Lin told her that her sister-in-law was going out. She was then taken by a group of people to a car waiting at the San Tai Wharf and driven to a location where she temporarily resided in the back room of a house. She was guarded by Lin, Li Xiuyu, and a thin man for about ten days, after which Lin ordered the two men to leave quickly, and she was able to escape. She did not know how much ransom was demanded, as it was all negotiated with her relatives, Wang Jiliang, and others. She has now returned to her hometown of Shaoxing. Detective Zhang Yunsheng stated that around 8 PM on the 19th, he and the detectives went to the Mengyuan Hotel on Hankou Road and obtained the bandit's phone number. He and the plaintiff's representative, surnamed Wang, went to the vicinity of the intersection of Edward Road and Jiangxi North Road. He disguised himself as a rickshaw puller and saw the defendant standing in the middle of Edward Road, wearing the gray silk robe presented as evidence and a Luo Song hat, talking to two men in suits, with his hands in his pockets, as if he was reaching for a gun. He had already heard gunshots. He stepped forward to arrest him, but he fled into the nearby Dechang Lane. There were wooden boxes piled up in the alley, and he feared that he would be ambushed. He was then able to escape. Detective Shang Wu stated that he saw the defendant in the middle of the road in front of the Anlegong Dance Hall on that road. He tried to restrain him, and gunshots rang out on both sides, knocking down two bandits. Dr. Guo Renji stated that the defendant came to the hospital for treatment on January 26th, using the alias Ma Gengsheng. He examined his wound and found that the bullet had already exited from his waist. There was no major problem. He stayed for sixteen days and was discharged after a full recovery. The medical expenses totaled $38.50. When questioned, the defendant stated that he had never been to Wang Yu's home. Jiang Dinghui invited him to the small hotel beforehand, saying that after this matter was completed, he would be given money to start a business. He went to Edward Road to be on the lookout and fled when he heard gunshots. He provided other evasive answers. Judge Shen ordered that he be returned to custody for further investigation.

[New Times for Shanghai-Songjiang Long-Distance Buses

▲ Effective from November 1st

Since the trial operation of the Shanghai-Songjiang Long-Distance Bus Company, the number of passengers has been increasing daily. However, the Huijiao Bridge at the Shanghai-Songjiang border has not yet been completed, preventing the official operation of the buses. The section from the Beiqiao Station to the Huijiao Bridge is being operated by borrowing vehicles from the Shanghai-Minhang Company. The company has set the new bus schedule to be effective from November 1st. The schedule is listed below: From Songjiang: 8:15 AM, 10:15 AM, 1:15 PM, 3:15 PM. From Shanghai: 8:30 AM, 10:30 AM, 1:30 PM, 3:30 PM. Passengers traveling from Shanghai to Songjiang should board the bus at the Shanghai Station of the Shanghai-Minhang Long-Distance Bus Company on Guohuo Road in the Nanshi district.

Privately Owned Cars Traveling on Shanghai-Minhang Road 145

▲ Fees will still be collected as usual.

The Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe Long-Distance Bus Company, which is managed by merchants, had allowed privately owned cars to pass through the Caohejing and Zhamen gates on the road for free since Double Ten Day due to the opening of the Jiang-Zhe Highway. However, the company is now concerned that the increasing number of vehicles is damaging the road surface, reducing its revenue, and increasing its expenditure on road maintenance. It feels that it cannot continue to make such sacrifices. Logically, car owners who benefit from using the road should fulfill their obligation to pay fees. This sentiment is shared by many Chinese and foreign residents. Therefore, starting from November 1st, privately owned cars traveling on the road for sightseeing or to the gardens on the Jiangbian side will still be charged fees as usual in order to maintain operations and compensate for losses.

Minhang Ferry Tolls 146

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction Minhang Ferry Management Office, located in Minhang Town, Shanghai, has been working day and night to ferry cars across the river, which is financially difficult and difficult to maintain. It has been decided that from November 1st, the ferry will operate as usual from 6 AM to 6 PM daily. After 6 PM, regardless of whether the cars are privately owned or commercially operated, the toll fee will be five yuan per vehicle. This announcement has already been posted at the ferry terminal.

Candy Vendor Angrily Strikes Child, Severing an Ear 148

Jiang Li, a 20-year-old woman from Gaoyou residing at No. 13, Youzhi Alley, Duojia Road, Nanshi District, usually makes a living by selling candy on the streets. Yesterday morning around 9 AM, she went out as usual to sell her candy. As she passed Qinglongge, a boy named Wen Qiyu (16 years old, from Tianjin), who lived nearby, came to her with a copper coin and wanted to play a dice game for candy. She rolled a five, and the boy rolled a six. According to the rules, the boy should have won, but she insisted that the boy only rolled a five, and the two began to argue. In a fit of anger, she raised her carrying pole and struck the boy on the head. The boy dodged, but was struck on the left ear, which was severed. Blood flowed profusely, and the boy cried out in pain. He Wenyi, the guard at the 31st post in the area, heard the commotion and rushed over. He first sent the boy to the hospital for treatment and then took the woman to the First District First Precinct. After a preliminary interrogation by the precinct chief, he transferred her to the Shanghai District Court for further investigation because the matter involved injury.
